10:T2d96a,<p><mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;" display="true"><mjx-math display="true" style="margin-left: 0; margin-right: 0;" class=" MJX-TEX"></mjx-math></mjx-container></p>
<p>The limit of a function describes the value that function approaches as its input approaches a certain value.</p>
<p>In formulas, the limit of a function is usually written as</p>
<p><mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;" display="true"><mjx-math display="true" style="margin-left: 0; margin-right: 0;" class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-munder><mjx-row><mjx-base style="padding-left: 0.014em;"><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c6C"></mjx-c><mjx-c class="mjx-c69"></mjx-c><mjx-c class="mjx-c6D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-base></mjx-row><mjx-row><mjx-under style="padding-top: 0.239em;"><mjx-TeXAtom size="s" texclass="ORD"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c2192"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D450 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-TeXAtom></mjx-under></mjx-row></mjx-munder><mjx-mi class="mjx-i" space="2"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D43F TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container></p>
<p>This formula describes the limit of <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-math></mjx-container> as <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container> approaches the constant <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D450 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container></p>

<div class="callout" data-callout="note">
<div class="callout-title">
<div class="callout-title-icon">
<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="lucide lucide-pencil"><path d="M17 3a2.85 2.83 0 1 1 4 4L7.5 20.5 2 22l1.5-5.5Z"/><path d="m15 5 4 4"/></svg>
</div>
<div class="callout-title-inner">Note</div>
</div>
<div class="callout-content"><p>It does not matter what the output of a function is or even if it exists for a limit to be taken.</p>
</div></div><p>Limits can also be taken from only one side meaning as the input variable approaches from either the left or right side of the graph it approaches a certain value. These limits are called <a href="One-Sided%20Limits">one-sided limit</a> and are useful when the limit at a point does not exist.</p>
<h1>Limitations</h1>
<p>For a limit to exist both sides of the value the input approaches must agree for example in the following function there does not exist a limit at <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mn class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c32"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container></p>

    </div><p>Using <a href="One-Sided%20Limits">one-sided limits</a> this limitation can be described as the limit of a function at a point does not exist if the left and right sided limits are not equal at that point.</p>

<p><mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;" display="true"><mjx-math display="true" style="margin-left: 0; margin-right: 0;" class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mtable style="min-width: 5.365em;"><mjx-table><mjx-itable><mjx-mtr><mjx-mtd style="text-align: right; padding-right: 0;"><mjx-munder><mjx-row><mjx-base style="padding-left: 0.038em;"><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c6C"></mjx-c><mjx-c class="mjx-c69"></mjx-c><mjx-c class="mjx-c6D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-base></mjx-row><mjx-row><mjx-under style="padding-top: 0.167em;"><mjx-TeXAtom size="s" texclass="ORD"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c2192"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c33"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-TeXAtom></mjx-under></mjx-row></mjx-munder><mjx-mi class="mjx-i" space="2"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-tstrut></mjx-tstrut></mjx-mtd><mjx-mtd style="text-align: left; padding-left: 0;"><mjx-mi class="mjx-n"></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mn class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c35"></mjx-c></mjx-mn><mjx-tstrut></mjx-tstrut></mjx-mtd></mjx-mtr></mjx-itable></mjx-table></mjx-mtable></mjx-math></mjx-container></p>
<blockquote>
<p>Notice how the limit at <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mn class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c33"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container> is <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c35"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container> even though the function <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-math></mjx-container> is defined to be <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c34"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container> at <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c33"></mjx-c></mjx-mn><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-math></mjx-container>. This is because the function approaches <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D466 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mn class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c35"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container> as <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container> approaches <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c33"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container>.</p>

<h2>Quotient Rule</h2>
<p><mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;" display="true"><mjx-math display="true" style="margin-left: 0; margin-right: 0;" class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-munder><mjx-row><mjx-base <p>Where <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D458 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container> is any constant number</p>
<h2>Power Rule</h2>

<h1>Calculating</h1>
<h2>Graphically</h2>
<p>One way to calculate a limit is to graph the function <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-math></mjx-container>. The limit of <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-math></mjx-container> is the value that the graph approaches as the input value. This can be seen graphically by looking at the values of the function as the input <em>gets closer</em> to the desired value.</p>
<p>For example given the following function the limit as <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container> approaches <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c33"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container> can be calculated using the following graph</p>

<h2>Numerically</h2>
<p>Another way to calculate a limit is to create a table of values that show the function evaluated at numbers that are close to the desired limit. The limit is the value that the function approaches as these numbers get closer to the desired limit.</p>
<p>For example given the following function the limit as <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container> approaches <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mn class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c33"></mjx-c></mjx-mn></mjx-math></mjx-container> can be calculated using the following table</p>

<h2>Symbolically</h2>
<p>We can also calculate the limit symbolically using algebraic techniques. This involves trying to simplify the function into an expression where the desired limit is easily visible.</p>
<h3>Methods</h3>
<h4>Direct Substitution</h4>
<p>For functions that are <a href="Continuous%20Function">continuous</a> at <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D44E TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-math></mjx-container> then the limit <mjx-container class="MathJax" jax="CHTML" style="font-size: 121%;"><mjx-math class=" MJX-TEX"><mjx-mstyle><mjx-munder><mjx-row><mjx-base style="padding-left: 0.048em;"><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c6C"></mjx-c><mjx-c class="mjx-c69"></mjx-c><mjx-c class="mjx-c6D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-base></mjx-row><mjx-row><mjx-under style="padding-top: 0.239em;"><mjx-TeXAtom size="s" texclass="ORD"><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c2192"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D44E TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi></mjx-TeXAtom></mjx-under></mjx-row></mjx-munder><mjx-mi class="mjx-i" space="2"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D465 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mo class="mjx-n" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c3D"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i" space="4"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D453 TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c28"></mjx-c></mjx-mo><mjx-mi class="mjx-i"><mjx-c class="mjx-c1D44E TEX-I"></mjx-c></mjx-mi><mjx-mo class="mjx-n"><mjx-c class="mjx-c29"></mjx-c></mjx-mo></mjx-mstyle></mjx-math></mjx-container>. Most limits solved symbolically re-arrange the equation such that direct substitution can be applied.</p>

</div></div><h4>Factoring and Simplifying</h4>
<p>The most common technique for calculating limits is by factorizing the function and removing any discontinuities.</p>

</div>
<div class="callout-title-inner">Example</div>
</div>

</div></div><h4>Rationalizing</h4>
<p>Sometimes rationalizing either the <strong>numerator</strong> or the <strong>denominator</strong> can help. Usually this only works for questions with radicals.</p>

<div class="callout" data-callout="example">
<div class="callout-title">
<div class="callout-title-icon">
<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="lucide lucide-list"><line x1="8" x2="21" y1="6" y2="6"/><line x1="8" x2="21" y1="12" y2="12"/><line x1="8" x2="21" y1="18" y2="18"/><line x1="3" x2="3.01" y1="6" y2="6"/><line x1="3" x2="3.01" y1="12" y2="12"/><line x1="3" x2="3.01" y1="18" y2="18"/></svg>
</div>
<div class="callout-title-inner">Example</div>
</div>

</div></div><h2>Alternative Approaches</h2>
<h4>L'Hôpital's Rule</h4>
<p><a href="L'H%C3%B4pital's%20Rule">L'Hôpital's rule</a> is a mathematical theorem that makes it possible to evaluate limits of an <a href="Indeterminate%20Form">indeterminate form</a>.</p>
<h4>The Squeeze Theorem</h4>
<p><a href="Squeeze%20Theorem">The squeeze theorem</a> is a mathematical theorem for finding the limit of a function trapped between two other functions.</p>
